</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture_and_media">Popular culture and media</span></h2>
<p>The 1974 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Houston,_We%27ve_Got_a_Problem" title="Houston, We've Got a Problem">Houston, We've Got a Problem</a></i>, while set around the Apollo 13 incident, is a fictional drama about the crises faced by ground personnel when the emergency disrupts their work schedules and places additional stress on their lives; only a couple of news clips and a narrator's solemn voice deal with the actual problems. "Houston... We've Got a Problem" was also the title of an episode of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> documentary series <i>A Life At Stake</i>, broadcast in March 1978. This was an accurate, if simplified, reconstruction of the events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lovell was approached in 1991 by journalist <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Kluger" title="Jeffrey Kluger">Jeffrey Kluger</a> about collaborating on a non-fiction account of the mission. The resultant book, <i><a href="/wiki/Lost_Moon" title="Lost Moon">Lost Moon: The Perilous Voyage of Apollo 13</a></i>, was published in 1994.
</p><p>The next year, in 1995, a film adaptation of the book, <i><a href="/wiki/Apollo_13_(film)" title="Apollo 13 (film)">Apollo 13</a></i>, was released, directed by <a href="/wiki/Ron_Howard" title="Ron Howard">Ron Howard</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a> as Lovell, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Paxton" title="Bill Paxton">Bill Paxton</a> as Haise, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Bacon" title="Kevin Bacon">Kevin Bacon</a> as Swigert, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Sinise" title="Gary Sinise">Gary Sinise</a> as Mattingly, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Harris" title="Ed Harris">Ed Harris</a> as <a href="/wiki/Flight_controller#FLIGHT" title="Flight controller">flight director</a> <a href="/wiki/Gene_Kranz" title="Gene Kranz">Gene Kranz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Quinlan" title="Kathleen Quinlan">Kathleen Quinlan</a> as Marilyn Lovell. James Lovell, Eugene Kranz, and other principals have stated that this film depicted the events of the mission with reasonable accuracy, given that some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dramatic_license" title="Dramatic license">dramatic license</a> was taken. For example, the film changes the tense of Lovell's famous follow-up to Swigert's original words from, "Houston, we've had a problem", to "<a href="/wiki/Houston,_we_have_a_problem" title="Houston, we have a problem">Houston, we have a problem</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-air2ground_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-air2ground-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The film was nominated for several Academy Awards, including Best Picture, Best Supporting Actor (Harris) and Best Supporting Actress (Quinlan).
</p><p>In the 1998 miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/From_the_Earth_to_the_Moon_(miniseries)" title="From the Earth to the Moon (miniseries)">From the Earth to the Moon</a></i>, co-produced by Hanks and Howard, the mission is dramatized in the episode "We Interrupt This Program". Rather than showing the incident from the crew's perspective as in the <i>Apollo 13</i> feature film, it is instead presented from an Earth-bound perspective of television reporters competing for coverage of the event.
</p><p>In 2008, an interactive theatrical show titled <i><a href="/wiki/Apollo_13:_Mission_Control" title="Apollo 13: Mission Control">Apollo 13: Mission Control</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> premiered at <a href="/wiki/BATS_Theatre" title="BATS Theatre">BATS Theatre</a> in Wellington, New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The production faithfully recreated the mission control consoles and audience members became part of the storyline. The show also featured a 'guest' astronaut each night: a member of the public who suited up and amongst other duties, stirred the oxygen tanks and said the line "Houston, we've had a problem." This 'replacement' astronaut was a nod to Jack Swigert, who replaced Ken Mattingly shortly before the launch in 1970. The production toured to other cities extensively in New Zealand and Australia in 2010–2011. The production was scheduled to travel to the US in 2012.
</p><p>In the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DC%27s_Legends_of_Tomorrow" title="DC's Legends of Tomorrow">DC's Legends of Tomorrow</a></i> episode 'Moonshot,' the oxygen tank explosion is averted when <a href="/wiki/Eobard_Thawne" title="Eobard Thawne">Eobard Thawne</a> disguises himself as Swigert, in order to retrieve a piece of the Spear of Destiny that was hidden in the pole section of the American flag planted on July 21, 1969. Thawne and <a href="/wiki/Atom_(Ray_Palmer)" title="Atom (Ray Palmer)">Ray Palmer</a> crash land the lander on the Moon's surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2011, a notebook containing a checklist Lovell used to calculate a trajectory to get the damaged spacecraft, Apollo 13, back to Earth, and handwritten calculations by Lovell, was auctioned off by <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Auctions" title="Heritage Auctions">Heritage Auctions</a> for $388,375. NASA made an email inquiry asking Heritage if Lovell had clear title to the notebook, stating that NASA had "nothing to indicate" the agency had ever transferred ownership of the checklist to Lovell. In January 2012, Heritage stated that the sale had been placed on hold after NASA launched an investigation into whether it was the astronaut's property to sell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
